URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS494426041	2020-02-28 18:05:05	5889	species	Baird's Sandpiper	Calidris bairdii			2				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Carson City	US-NV-510		9			Carson City WWTP Wetlands	L868854	H	39.1638915	-119.7365785	2017-04-16	13:16:00	obsr630400	S36040593	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	66	1.770		2	1	G2343730	1	1	1			In the field, Emma and I noted two larger birds with longer wings, but the flocks flushed and we decided to look at pictures of them later. We only came back to the pictures now and determined they were actually Baird's Sandpipers (our initial thought was that they might be Westerns, but the much larger size and longer wings pointed against that. Western has been shockingly absent here for us). There are two birds which I call bird 1 and bird 2. Both are significantly larger than Least Sandpipers, larger in comparison than a Western Would be, with long wings, long straight bills, and it appears to be dark legs. Bird 1 is slightly grayer and seems less patterned, whereas Bird 2 seems browner, but overall they look similar structurally and in terms of size. We only came back to the pictures now and determined they were actually Baird's Sandpipers (our initial thought was that they might be Westerns, but the much larger size and longer wings pointed against that. Western has been shockingly absent here for us). There are two birds which I call bird 1 and bird 2. Both are significantly larger than Least Sandpipers, larger in comparison than a Western Would be, with long wings, long straight bills, and it appears to be dark legs. Bird 1 is slightly grayer and seems less patterned, whereas Bird 2 seems browner, but overall they look similar structurally and in terms of size.
